<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="a6c6b0fb81c84d838d13630e8c1d756e">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'be59b59d-a18e-4f0d-93b2-01c020497a54'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d143763065" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>The high irreversibility to FeS<sub>2</sub>-based anode thwarts its applicability in sodium ion batteries (SIBs), originally stem from the sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction kinetics, confined by the high desolvation barrier, the thick electric double layer (EDL) and the long transport routine inside FeS<sub>2</sub>. Herein, the covalent polypeptide oligomers (Pcy) based on cysteine (Cy) with β-sheet configuration grafted binary hollow carbon coupled FeS<sub>2</sub>@Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> heterostructure, i.e., FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, are designed to achieve low desolvation barrier, the contracted EDL via weakened coulombic interaction stems from the zwitterionic feature and enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> transport capacity inside FeS<sub>2</sub>. The semi-interpenetrating oligomers possessing a weak coordination environment, massively accelerate the desolvation kinetics, additionally, the orderly and dense vertical occupation within the inner Helmholtz plane (IHP) also enormously reduces thickness of EDL. The binary hollow structure complex possessing typical ion looping routine considerably expedites the Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics inside anode. Both experimental and theoretical trials demonstrate such FeS<sub>2</sub> composite manifests a high reversibility in Na<sup>+</sup> storage in virtue of exceptional structure stability, rapid ion transport kinetics, and swift reaction kinetics.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403489-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403489-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been witnessed to be an alternative upgrade candidate for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0001_R_d143763057e390" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - SmartMat">1</a>-<a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0004_R_d143763057e390" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nano-Micro Lett.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> transition metal sulfides (TMSs) are a delicate carrier for SIBs due to their enriched sources, reaction diversity, and high theoretical capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0005_R_d143763057e395" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv. Energy Mater.">5</a>-<a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0008_R_d143763057e395" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Particularly, comparing with carbonaceous anode, the voltage platform of TMSs exceeds 1.0&nbsp;V, which can avoid the generation of metal dendrite and demonstrate the high safety advantages. These fascinating advantages manifests that TMSs can be the attractive candidates for next-generation energy upgradation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0009_R_d143763057e400" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Acta Phys.-Chim. Sin.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Among these TMSs choices, FeS<sub>2</sub> is a promising insertion involved anode material with a high theoretical capacity and an abundant source.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0010_R_d143763057e408" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - eScience">10</a>-<a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0012_R_d143763057e408" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Small Sci.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, the disadvantage of high irreversibility in SIBs over FeS<sub>2</sub> results in the sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction kinetics due to the large volume variation for Na<sup>+</sup> storage, mainly subjected to the hysteresis Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics including the paramount desolvation barrier, and the loose and thick shielding solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer derived from the poor interface compatibility, and the high activation barrier resulting in the incompletely conversion of intermediates,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0013_R_d143763057e422" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">13</a>-<a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0016_R_d143763057e422" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Energy Storage Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> ceaseless electrolyte consume, and serious structure deformation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0017_R_d143763057e427" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Chem. Eng. J.">17</a>-<a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0020_R_d143763057e427" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For governing the huge volume expansion in order to avoid structure pulverization and rapid capacity fading during repetitive cycling, many exception work such as carbon hybridization and nanotechnology protocols have been reported to conquer the above challenges.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0021_R_d143763057e433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - ACS Nano">21</a>-<a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0024_R_d143763057e433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Rare Met.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To this end, the rending of carbon-based porous materials especially the 3D crosslinked conductive network facilitates rapid electron/ion transport, mitigates volumetric expansion, and simultaneously helps to build condensed SEI film.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0025_R_d143763057e438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nat. Commun.">25</a>, <a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0026_R_d143763057e438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Small">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The nanosized engineering is also an effective strategy for strengthening structural stability and electrochemical behaviors of TMSs anode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0027_R_d143763057e443" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a>, <a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0028_R_d143763057e443" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Energy Storage Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Excluding the inorganic guest of carbonaceous moiety, the construction of a functional elastomer interlayer can enhance the structure integrity, promote ion transport within electrolyte, expediting the reaction kinetics toward the full conversion of intermediates into Na<sub>2</sub>S.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0029_R_d143763057e452" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - ACS Nano">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The organic moiety is required to satisfy coherence and adherence between the anode electrode and the cladding in order to avoid the formation of stiff interface, preventing its peeling of electrode from collector.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0030_R_d143763057e457" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, the synchronized motion of cations with anions enables the uneven distribution of Na-ion flux and the generation of a space-charge region at the anode metal interface, and eventually results in the uneven Na deposition and the mechanical failure over SEI.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0031_R_d143763057e463" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Energy Environ. Sci.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Up to present, typical protein complex was reported to induce planar ion deposition and construct stable SEI layer, such as silk fibroin-polyvinyl alcohol,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0032_R_d143763057e468" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - ACS Nano">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> silk fibroin,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0033_R_d143763057e473" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Mater. Chem. A">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> collagen protein,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0034_R_d143763057e479" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Sci. Adv.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and zein protein.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0035_R_d143763057e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Energy Storage Mater.">35</a>, <a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0036_R_d143763057e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Biotechnol. Adv.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The synergistic effects of the electrostatic interaction with the negative species in the inner Helmholtz plane (IHP), the positive species in the out Helmholtz plane (OHP) result in thinner electric double layer (EDL), benefitting from the avoid of conventional large solvated molecule clusters, considerably shortening the Na<sup>+</sup> transport routine inside electrolyte and reducing the desolvation kinetics.</p>
         
         <p>For expediting the reaction kinetics, charge-density polarization affords as critical guidelines that supply perspective into the <i>d</i>-electron filling states and serve the descriptor of the structure-property relationship, unveiling why protocols, such as those that build heterojunctions and dope, are effective for lowering the active barrier.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0037_R_d143763057e496" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">37</a>, <a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0014_R_d143763057e496" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Adv. Energy Mater.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Heterojunction structure stimulates charge transfer and electron polarization at the interface, eventually giving rise to a variation in the antibonding states accompanied by a downshifting or upshifting of the <i>d</i>-band center.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0038_R_d143763057e503" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Likewise, elemental doping can impact activation and influence the conductivity of FeS<sub>2</sub> composite, serving as a pivotal factor for electrochemical processes.</p>
         
         <p>Herein, the well-assembled covalent polypeptides aggregate based on polypeptide oligomers (Pcy) were rendered to graft the binary hollow carbon nested heterostructure FeS<sub>2</sub>@Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanospheres (NPs), the fabricated FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy composites was evaluated for glorious Na<sup>+</sup> storage towards high reversibility, excellent rate and cycling behaviors. The fabrication of higher order supramolecular through intersected Pcy, structurally stabled zwitterionic FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanostructure with high sodiophilicity and strong binding energy to Na<sup>+</sup>, massively holds structure integrity, expedites ion transport kinetics, and accelerates the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/exfoliation kinetics. Pcy with polar groups supply high dipole moments and conjugation via disulfide bridge to fabricate topologic topology structures, offering extra voids to accommodate huge volume variation, and decreasing the local current to prevent the vertical Na deposition. A compacted and thinner IHP of EDL is achieved to bolster Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics because of the facile pulling tendency of Na<sup>+</sup> with anions. The topologic buffer layer displays higher mechanical strength to promote a polar molecular layer, uniform Na deposition, and thus ultralong cycling longevity. The heterojunction of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy on the premise of the electron transfer from C to S with the O bridge considerably increases the unpaired electrons of Fe based on the medium spin state (MS), the evident attenuation of conversion reaction barrier, and the rapid Na<sup>+</sup> imbedding/exfoliation kinetics with a high reversibility consequently.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403489-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403489-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>After partial vulcanization over Fe@C, the heterojunction structure of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C was obtained (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0001">1a</a>). Remarkably, cysteine (Cy) inclines to assemble into the right-handed α-helices structure driven by enthalpy-preferred peptide condensation, and then fabricates into β-sheet via hydrogen bonding, involved in allosteric property from α-helices to β-sheet. Such β-sheet configuration was confirmed by circular dichroism spectra (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). Unlike the α-helix configuration, interchain hydrogen bonds are formed among Pcy molecules, which are nearly perpendicular to the long axis of Pcy, and the chain of Pcy is almost completely extended (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information). The atomic distance between Cy with the α-helix is 15.886 Å while the atomic distance between Pcy is 18.731 Å nearly with a fully extended state. Additionally, a new peak plotted at 196&nbsp;nm is noticed in circular dichroism spectra, which is contributed to the β-sheet signal.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0039_R_d143763057e581" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Biomacromolecules.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403489-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/bd4df704-bbb4-4868-821b-a1cc20cf7eac/aenm202403489-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/bd4df704-bbb4-4868-821b-a1cc20cf7eac/aenm202403489-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/fbe59696-131e-4736-a57e-f35d2dcbb578/aenm202403489-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/bd4df704-bbb4-4868-821b-a1cc20cf7eac/aenm202403489-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403489-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403489" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The schematic synthesis process of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy (upward), schematic diagram of the evolution of Pcy (downward). b) The SEM image, c,d) the TEM image, e) the SAED image, f) the HRTEM image, g) the EDX image, h) the XRD profile of FeS<sub>2</sub> complexes. i) Schematic illustration of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy prepared by secondary intercalation method.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Excellent mechanical rigidity and flexibility can be approached, benefitting from such configuration conversion, in which the stronger breaking strength and larger breaking elongation is noticed for Pcy (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). Based on the successful synthesis of Fe-C NPs (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>,&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information), the binary yolk-shell Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C was obtained after calcination at 500 °C (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>,&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information), the well-preserved yolk-shell shape were well inherited by FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C after incomplete vulcanization (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information). Remarkably, the pore structure became more obvious due to etching via H<sub>2</sub>S during the above vulcanization process, which is beneficial for supplying more active cites and the infiltration of the electrolyte (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information). FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy has a typical mesoporous structure with a pore size distribution between 3 and 6&nbsp;nm. The high porosity and high specific surface area of the microstructure are conducive to the uniform deposition of sodium ions and the rapid transfer of ions/electrons during charging and discharging. After the condensation reaction after thermal treatment in Cy, FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C was closely entangled by self-assembled Pcy multilayers, forming urchin-like polypeptide oligomers (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0001">1b–d</a>) with the polycrystalline feature (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0001">1e</a>) and the continuous ion conductive porous framework. Each constituent including Fe, C, O, S, N uniformly distribute within the whole backbone of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0001">1f,g</a>). Remarkably, the progressively increased interlamellar spacing of FeS<sub>2</sub> is achieved after the coupling of carbon and Pcy, in which the enlarged spacing for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> from 0.272 to 0.288&nbsp;nm is noticed stem from the weakened π–π stacking force (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0001">1h,i</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0040_R_d143763057e699" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Pcy plays a pivotal role of pillar over FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, preventing the collapse and pulverization during the repeated sodium stripping/plating process. Pcy with a β-sheet configuration serving as FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C solid-ion conductors are endowed some plastic deformation,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0041_R_d143763057e719" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Nat. Commun.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> moderate rigidity and elasticity, indicating more favorable mechanical stress to encumber the puncture effect of SEI. FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is entrusted by the exceptional mechanical behaviors via the rigid-flexible protein moiety. After grafting with Pcy, the condensation of Pcy was authenticated by the inherently damped singles of the asymmetric and symmetric stretching vibration peaks of ─COOH at 1397 and 1600&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, the fading signals of bending vibration and stretching vibration peaks at 1538 and 3449&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> of ─NH<sub>2</sub>, respectively. The newly appeared peaks at 1630, 3715, 2070&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, are well indexed to be ─C═O, NH<sub>2</sub><sup>+</sup>, and S─S peaks (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). In the regard, the nearest-neighbor bilayer of Pcy coordinates with Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> through covalent disulfide bridge formation between Pcy and FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C in the ordered inner and dense outer pattern, which is facilitated to the dipole effect in the inner of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C, resulting in the ordered self-assembled protein-particle building blocks.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0042_R_d143763057e763" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Sustain Chem. Eng.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Reading from the dramatic declined contact angles from 51.2° to 28.6° (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information), the sodiophilicity of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is considerably enhanced via such sequential coordination of Pcy to promote the planar Na deposition. The successful preparation of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy was also corroborated by the co-current flow of the E<sub>g</sub> and A<sub>g</sub> models of FeS<sub>2</sub>, the A<sub>g1</sub>, E<sub>g2+g3</sub>, and E<sub>g4</sub> models of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information), the D and G models of C, the generation of Fe─O─C atomic bonds. According to the analysis of ICP-OES and thermal analysis, the weight percentages of FeS<sub>2</sub>, Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, C, and Pcy are 65.2%, 9.9%, 13.4%, and 11.5% (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information), respectively. Additionally, the successful chemical cooperation of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C with Pcy is backed by appearance of Fe─O─C, and the red shift of S 2p and Fe 2p spectra in XPS profile (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information). The characteristic peaks of O 1s of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy can be fitted into three peaks, which are C═O (530.3&nbsp;eV), Fe─O─C (531.7&nbsp;eV) and C─O (533.1&nbsp;eV) bonds, respectively. For the high-resolution spectrum of C 1s, and the total peaks can be fitted to C─C (283.9&nbsp;eV), C─N/C─S (285.0&nbsp;eV), C─O (285.9&nbsp;eV), and C═O (286.3&nbsp;eV) bonds, where the occurrence of C─N/C─S groups indicates a tight connection between cysteine, carbon nanosheets, and bivalve FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanospheres. The three fitting peaks of the N 1s high-resolution spectrum are located at 399.3, 401.1, and 402.1&nbsp;eV, respectively, corresponding to pyridine nitrogen, pyrrole nitrogen, and graphite nitrogen. In the S 2p high-resolution spectra of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, the characteristic peaks can be fitted to four peaks at 161.3, 162.7, 164.3, and 168.6&nbsp;eV, which are attributed to S<sup>2−</sup>, C─S, and C─SO<sub>x</sub> bonds, respectively. Compared with the FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C, the S<sup>2−</sup> characteristic peak in FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is transferred to the high-energy region, and its binding energy change value is ∆E<sub>1</sub> = 0.29&nbsp;eV, ∆E<sub>2</sub> = 0.39&nbsp;eV, indicating that the electrons are transferred from sulfur to metal. For Fe 2p high-resolution spectra of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, the two characteristic peaks at 706.5 and 717.7&nbsp;eV are attributed to Fe<sup>2+</sup>, while the two peaks at 707.9 and 719.5&nbsp;eV are caused by Fe<sup>3+</sup>. Compared with the FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C, the Fe<sup>2+</sup> and Fe<sup>3+</sup> characteristic peaks contained in Fe 2p<sub>3/2</sub> in FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy were transferred to the low-energy region, and their binding energy variation values were ∆E<sub>1</sub> = −0.30&nbsp;eV, ∆E<sub>2</sub> = −0.22&nbsp;eV, indicating an increase in the electron cloud density near ferric sulfide. FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is expected to demonstrate superior electrochemical performance, benefiting from the favorable rigid-elastic feature, the binary hollow heterojunction structure, the smart composition design.</p>
         
         <p>The typical advances of the discussed FeS<sub>2</sub> complexes in morphology, solvation environment, and the thickness of EDL were investigated and discussed. The enriched Na<sup>+</sup>-Pcy-aggregated ion pairs over FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy are noticed towards the fine Na planar deposition (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2a</a>). Noticeably, the feasible dissociation tendency of ─SH and ─COOH gives rise to the zwitterionic property for Pcy derived from the relative minimum binding energy of ─SH and ─COOH with Pcy (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information). Remarkably, the weak coulombic interactions of Na<sup>+</sup> with zwitterionic Pcy, and the immobilization interaction of Pcy with ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>, endow the facile extraction tendency of Na<sup>+</sup> out of the first sheath of Na<sup>+</sup>-Pcy-ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup> and thus the rapid Na<sup>+</sup> transport capacity. By dramatic contrast, a high ratio of solvent separated ion pairs (SSIP) is achieved for bulk FeS<sub>2</sub>, leading to thick, loose SEI and the uneven Na deposition (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2b</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0043_R_d143763057e958" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">43</a>, <a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0044_R_d143763057e958" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Adv. Mater.">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Reading from larger coordination distance for Na/O over Pcy (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2c,d</a>), FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy exhibits a weaker solvated environment because of the higher binding energy of Pcy-ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup> in contrast to that of Na-ClO<sub>4</sub>, Na-Pcy (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information), which efficiently fixes the anions and substantially accelerates the Na<sup>+</sup> transport capacity. Thereby, the modification of Pcy expedites the desolvation of NaClO<sub>4</sub> toward the growing tendency to twist and break over the bond of O─O in ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>. Remarkably, the coordination numbers of Na<sup>+</sup> with O over ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup> reduce from the initial 1.6 to 1.1, respectively, but for PC and FEC decrease from the original 4.0, 1.3 to 0, 1.2, respectively. The largest coordination number of Na<sup>+</sup> with O over Pcy is 2. The coordination number with Na<sup>+</sup> is in following sequence: Pcy &gt; PC &gt; FEC &gt; ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>. To be in line with the above discussions, the large amounts of aggregated ion pairs and contact ion pairs were harvested for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, by contrast, the separated solvent ion pairs are concentrated over FeS<sub>2</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2e</a>). Except for the preferable weaker solvation environment, the dislocated electrons are noticed because of the built-in electric field and the hybrid of electron negative N, S, P over Pcy, in which the enriched electrons concentrate on the interface boundary of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, which are favorable for the Na<sup>+</sup> trapping (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2f</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information) and also expedites the Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetic behaviors, which is beneficial for the impinge of heterogeneous Na stacking via the electrostatic repulsion force and the immobilization of dissolved S<sub>x</sub> species, which can substantially enhance the Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics in electrolyte.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403489-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/53810fbc-071c-4242-9c1b-a87fbfcc7000/aenm202403489-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/53810fbc-071c-4242-9c1b-a87fbfcc7000/aenm202403489-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8db8876f-0124-442d-a8ce-add3183e0b4e/aenm202403489-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/53810fbc-071c-4242-9c1b-a87fbfcc7000/aenm202403489-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403489-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403489" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">MD simulation snapshots and corresponding Na<sup>+</sup>-solvation structure of a) FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy and b) FeS<sub>2</sub>. Na<sup>+</sup> intermolecular radical distribution Functions (RDFs) of c) FeS<sub>2</sub> and d) FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy. e) The proportion of different solvation structures of the FeS<sub>2</sub> complexes. f) The electron local function diagram and differential charge density diagram of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy. g) Corresponding EDL capacitance. h) Calculated ESP distribution, i) frontier molecular orbital energy level of NaClO<sub>4</sub> and Pcy-NaClO<sub>4</sub>. j) The Na<sup>+</sup> concentration profiles and Na metal deposition at the selected simulation time. k) The stress distribution of FeS<sub>2</sub> (left) and FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy (right).</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The EDL experimental results showed the IHP of such FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C anode was almost occupied by PC and FEC molecules. Consequently, the capacitance of the EDL (C<sub>d</sub>) is kept almost unaltered. Nevertheless, after rendering Pcy composition, the initial increment and the subsequent decrement of Pcy in the IHP are noticed, promoting the conversion of Pcy from parallel to vertical adsorption along the electrode interface (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403489-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403489-bib-0045_R_d143763057e1115" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Energy Storage Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The vertical adsorption of Pcy takes responsible for the harvested C<sub>d</sub> gap between FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C and FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy. The larger spatial hindrance of Pcy and its self-assembly lead the reconstruction within the IHP layer, giving rise to the orderly and dense vertical orientation in IHP and isolating solvent molecules from the anode surface to inhibit the excess decomposition of these organic species and weaken the EDL repulsive force of Na<sup>+</sup> to a greater extent (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2g</a>). At this point, the primary adsorption of Pcy along the vertical direction is also backed by the higher binding energy of Pcy rather than PC, FEC with FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18b</a>, Supporting Information). Based on the graft of Pcy, the enlarged corrosion potential values (Ecorr) from 0.103 to 0.271&nbsp;V and the diminished corrosion current (Icorr) manifest Pcy-containing EDL exerted a physical barrier to inhibit the reaction between sodium and FeS<sub>2</sub> and the lower Na nucleus over potential (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information). Simultaneously, the condensed EDL stem from predominated occupancy of Pcy in IHP, and the left solvents species in the OHP render the expedited Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics through SEI. Combining the rapid desolvation kinetics and the accelerated both interface and solid-state Na<sup>+</sup> transport process over FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, the conversion reaction of FeS<sub>2</sub> was by substantially expedited.</p>
         
         <p>The coordination interactions among Pcy, Na<sup>+</sup>, and ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>/solvents were also uncovered by electrostatic potential (ESP) calculations (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2h</a>). The dense charge density of Pcy over FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy than FeS<sub>2</sub> is harvested by the obvious color contrast for ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup> between Pcy-Na<sup>+</sup>(ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>) and Na<sup>+</sup>(ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>). Consistently, the graft of Pcy with FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy reduces the LUMO of Pcy-NaClO<sub>4</sub>, which is favorable for the produce of inorganic NaF pre-dominated SEI, substantially accelerating the desolvation kinetics behaviors (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2i</a>). In comparing with FeS<sub>2</sub>, the decreased band gap of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is visualized, indicating the considerably increased electron conductivity and strengthened electron transport capability via the built-in electric field bridged by Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. Based on the promoted electron delocalization around the Fermi level (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information), the elongated and the twisted Fe-S can be achieved because of the primary coordination of Fe with N and O via the atomic Fe─N─C and Fe─O─C, further implying the declined activation barrier of FeS<sub>2</sub> involved in insertion and conversion reactions. The affinity of ─COOH, ─NH<sub>2</sub>, and ─SH with Na<sup>+</sup> leads the massively homogenized Na<sup>+</sup> flux and the even Na deposition (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2j</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information). Excepted for the enhanced interface compatibility, the considerably released stress is also noticed over FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy via orderly oriented Pcy and binary hollow structure of FeS<sub>2</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0002">2k</a>), greatly expedites the Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics in bulk electrode. The speeded Na<sup>+</sup> transport capacity in solvent, SEI, and electrode entrusts the accelerated Na<sup>+</sup> embedding/exfoliation kinetics.</p>
         
         <p>Based on the fine infusion of ionic/electric conductive composition, and the ingenious interface feature, the rapid Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics, FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is expected to manifest the most preeminent reversibly in SIBs. Carefully compared the initial galvanostatic charge/discharge curves of FeS<sub>2</sub> based complexes at a current density of 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>, FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy delivers an initial discharge capacity of ≈834.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (volumetric capacity is 1518 mAh cm<sup>−3</sup>) with an initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 90.3% (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0003">3a</a>), surpasses those of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C (≈820.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, 84.2%), FeS<sub>2</sub> (≈568.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, 82.4%) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a>, Supporting Information). C, and Pcy deliver the charge capacities of 135.2, 38.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, indicating the paramount capacity contribution from FeS<sub>2</sub>. The increment of electron conductivity due to the addition of C and the shaping of heterojunction of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C, the adjacent extra active sites from ─COOH, ─NH<sub>2</sub>, and ─SH active sites (C═OO···Na<sup>+</sup>, S···Na<sup>+</sup>, ─N···Na<sup>+</sup>) contribute greatly to the large capacity for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy. Noticeably, the intimate encapsulation of Pcy isolates the electrolyte with FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy and prohibits the parasitic reaction between electrode and electrolyte.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403489-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5fba0a54-4bb0-48ff-859f-fb756972d6ed/aenm202403489-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/5fba0a54-4bb0-48ff-859f-fb756972d6ed/aenm202403489-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8390b8bb-b637-430f-a87f-3be5f4be651a/aenm202403489-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5fba0a54-4bb0-48ff-859f-fb756972d6ed/aenm202403489-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403489-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403489" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The galvanostatic discharge/charge curves for the initial five cycles at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy. b) 3D rendering visualization of the selected secondary-ion fragments of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (upper) and FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy (lower). c) Depth profile curves of TOF-SIMs, d) Cycling performance of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C and FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> for 100 cycles. e) Cycling performance of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup> for 1000 cycles. f) AFM topography images and g) Modulus distribution of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy (left) and FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C (right). h,i) In situ XRD profiles of the FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy electrode.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>After the first discharging/charging, the generated of SEI including component/penetration/distribution was screened. For FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, the thin and dense SEI layer with inorganic-abundant NaF and Na<sub>2</sub>O facilitates the thwart of parasite reactions between electrode and electrolyte and rapid Na<sup>+</sup> migration (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0003">3b,c</a>). These inorganic series are more plotted on the surface of electrode, while the organic counterpart tends to concentrate within the inner SEI. For FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, the widely penetrated inorganic/organic species over FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> implies the loose and thick SEI layer (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>In comparing with FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C, FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy manifested a glorious adaptation to all current densities. With 100 times increment of current density from 0.05 to 5 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24a,b</a>, Supporting Information), a low-capacity degeneration of 32.2% was manifested for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy. The high-rate performance is still preserved at a higher current density of 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, a high capacity of ≈475.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> was achieved by FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy anode with a recuperative capacity of ≈691.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> when the current density got back to 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>, demonstrating an average coulombic efficiency (CE) of 99.3%. By a sharp contrast, both FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C manifest an obvious capacity attenuation, especially for that of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, only 19.6% of its original capacity was retained at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy also delivered outstanding cycling behaviors. Remarkably, after 100 cycles at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0003">3d</a>), a high capacity of ≈683.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> was maintained for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, corresponding to ≈88.7% of its pristine capacity, higher than those of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C (≈70.2% capacity preservation). Even under a more oppressive current rate of 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, ≈81.7% of its pristine capacity was delivered for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy after uninterrupted 500 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0003">3e</a>).</p>
         
         <p>Thanks for the graft of β-sheet Pcy with remarking mechanical strength, the more smooth surface of SEI layer and a larger Young's modulus of 7.2&nbsp;GPa for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy are noticed after 500 cycles, and the uneven surface of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C and smaller Young's modulus of 4.4&nbsp;GPa further prove the even and ingenious mechanical strength of SEI layer (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0003">3f,g</a>), the more atomically flat surface and larger Young's modulus, adhesive force are approached for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy, by contrast, the coarse and rugged contour for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C is witnessed. In this regard, the more free voids offered by fluffy Pcy and binary hollow structure of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> can massively mitigate the large volume variation due to the Na<sup>+</sup> plating/stripping process. Such FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy demonstrates the most outstanding rate and cycling behaviors and commendable volumetric capacity compared with other FeS<sub>2</sub> based anode previously reported up to date (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24c,d</a>, Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). At this point, the elastic Pcy oligomers grafted FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> complexes with enriched voids due to the urchin-like hollow binary yolk-shell structure can sufficiently release the stress produced during the Na<sup>+</sup> expansion/extraction process, the well-tailored interface compatibility due to the 3D backbone, the homogenized Na<sup>+</sup> flux and most important, the condensed IHP in EDL to promote the even Na deposition, the cut-off side reaction due to isolation of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy from the electrolyte via Pcy take responsible. The promoted formation of stable solid electrolyte interface (SEI) due to the depressed local current density and homogenized Na<sup>+</sup> flux via polar groups and coupled by the enhanced electron transport via the build-in electric field formed between FeS<sub>2</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> cooperatively also improve the long durable cycling behaviors of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy. The well inherited urchin-like binary hollow structure integrity of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is achieved after 500 cycles, while the crumpling of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C with large amounts of fragments are noticed for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, the self-repairing of the polypeptide framework with high mobility also contributes to the excellent longevity of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy via breaking and recombination of hydrogen bonds over Pcy to repair the structure deformation for Na<sup>+</sup> storage (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a>,&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a>, Supporting Information). In the regard, the severance and recombination of hydrogen bonds over Pcy during the self-repairing process was also collected and corroborated (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information). The weak H-bond remarkably increases when subjecting scratching and the recovery of the strong H-bond when the structure deformation is finished, implying that the effective alteration among the initial HB network to harvest the self-adaptive capacity. Particularly, the superior rate and cycling performance is also related to the suppressed S shuttle effect. A concurrent anchoring/converting strategy is presented to restrain the dissolution of Na<sub>x</sub>S<sub>y</sub> and realize the rapid conversion of intermediates (Na<sub>x</sub>S<sub>y</sub>) to Na<sub>2</sub>S. A prototypical regulator constitutes of polar Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> catalysts embedded in the hollow matrix (i.e., FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy), which endows fast electron/ion transportation and inhibits shuttle effects, i.e., the strong physical/chemical adsorption as well as chemical catalysis methodologies. Detailedly, Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> as redox accelerator entrusts the stretched S-S bonds to decrease the Na<sub>x</sub>S<sub>y</sub> bidirectional conversion barrier, achieving accelerated reaction kinetics. In the visualized Na<sub>2</sub>S<sub>6</sub> adsorption measurement (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a>, Supporting Information), the red brown color of Na<sub>2</sub>S<sub>6</sub> solution becomes almost colorless with the FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy dispersion, reflecting its high adsorption ability to polysulfides. Thereafter, the supernatants after the adsorption experiments were collected, diluted, and analyzed by UV–vis spectrometry. The peak at ∼340&nbsp;nm in the absorption spectrum is attributed to the absorption of S<sub>6</sub><sup>2−</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a>, Supporting Information). Thanks for the synergistic effects of the high porosity of interconnected matrix and the strong chemisorption of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, the extremely low S<sub>6</sub><sup>2−</sup> adsorption intensity of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy indicates its strong adsorption capacity to polysulfides. The polysulfides can thus be confined inside of pores of host materials, chemically anchored, and effectively converse to Na<sub>2</sub>S as a consequent. In the regard, the rational medium spin state of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy enables the moderate adsorption of intermediates derived from the lower occupation of anti-σ orbit, and thus the rapid conversion intermediate polysulfides to Na<sub>2</sub>S (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31</a>, Supporting Information), which was also backed by the lower acitivation barrier of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>The involved redox reactions of FeS<sub>2</sub> over FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy were studied via cyclic voltammograms (CV) and in situ XRD profiles. The CV curves of the FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy anode investigated within the voltage range of 0.01 to 3.0&nbsp;V at a scan rate of 0.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> were further calcified and discussed accordingly. The sharp anodic peak observed at 0.93&nbsp;V is associated with the formation of Na<sub>x</sub>FeS<sub>2</sub> (0 &lt; x ≤ 2), which is closely related with the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> into FeS<sub>2</sub>, accompanied by the generation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S33a,b</a>, Supporting Information). The subsequent peak detected at 0.3&nbsp;V is indicative of further conversion and alloying reactions, leading to the formation of metallic Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S. Furthermore, the cathodic peak at 0.01&nbsp;V is characteristic of the (de)intercalation of solvated Na<sup>+</sup> into the carbon matrix within the ester-based electrolyte. The oxidation peak at 1.45&nbsp;V is noteworthy, as it illustrates the multistep desodiation process of Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S, culminating in the formation of Na<sub>2-x</sub>FeS<sub>2</sub>. Additionally, a broad cathodic peak is discernible at 2.5&nbsp;V, which is ascribed to the sodiation reaction of the intermediary Na<sub>x</sub>FeS<sub>2</sub>. Specifically, the cathodic/anodic peaks observed in subsequent cycles are assigned to the reversible reactions between Na<sub>2-x</sub>FeS<sub>2</sub> and Fe, Na<sub>2</sub>S. The glorious reversibility of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is also validated by the fine overlay of 2nd and 3rd loop, benefiting from the alleviated side reaction between electrolyte and electrode derived from Pcy. The CV profiles of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C is similar with that of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy except for the larger voltage polarization because of the lack of C and Pcy in decreasing irreversible reactions, assisting in improving the interface compatibility and the redox kinetics (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S33c</a>, Supporting Information). To be in line with the result of CV profiles, a series of in situ tests were conducted within the potential range of 0.01 to 3.0&nbsp;V. In the open circuit voltage state, the peaks at 33.0° and 40.8° observed in the fresh cell correspond to the (200) and (211) planes of FeS<sub>2</sub>. As the potential is discharged to ≈0.8&nbsp;V, the peaks attributed to FeS<sub>2</sub> gradually diminish, and peaks indicative of NaFeS<sub>2</sub>, resulting from interphase transformation, emerge at 30.85° and 38.2°; this stage signifies an intercalation process involving Na<sup>+</sup> and FeS<sub>2</sub>. With continued discharging to 0.01&nbsp;V, the diffraction peaks of NaFeS<sub>2</sub> disappear, accompanied by the appearance of new peaks at ≈38.96° and 46.1°, which correspond to the Na<sub>2</sub>S phase and suggest further sodiation of the NaFeS<sub>2</sub> phase during this period. Meanwhile, the peaks associated with the FeS<sub>2</sub> phase also vanish given when fully discharged. However, to be consistent with previous studies, the corresponding diffraction peaks of metallic Fe were not observed in this process, possibly due to its low crystallinity. As further charged to 1.8&nbsp;V, the NaFeS<sub>2</sub> phase re-emerges, exhibiting weakened peak signals at ≈46°, revealing the conversion reaction from NaFeS<sub>2</sub> to Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S. Subsequently, upon fully charged to 3.0&nbsp;V, the byproduct Na<sub>2</sub>S phase completely vanishes, indicating a reversible conversion reaction between FeS<sub>2</sub> and Na<sup>+</sup>. It is worth noting that no peaks corresponding to the FeS<sub>2</sub> phase was detected when fully charged, implying a fully conversion from FeS<sub>2</sub> to NaFeS<sub>2</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0003">3h,i</a>).</p>
         
         <p>The diffusion kinetics was also illustrated via by the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S34</a>, Supporting Information), in which the higher diffusion coefficient of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is noticed in contrast to FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C, FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy also manifests the low ion/electron transfer resistance in EIS analysis (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S35</a>, Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). Based on dedicated structural/compositional fabrication strategy, the rapid kinetics of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy is also the proved by the high ratio pseudocapacitive contribution in contrast to surface capacity contribution (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S36</a>, Supporting Information). The pseudocapacitive contribution ratio to the total capacity for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy achieves to ≈90.2% at a scanning rate of 1.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, implying the pseudo-capacitive controlled Na<sup>+</sup> storage process, which is higher than that of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C ≈77.2% in the same situation (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S37</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>Benefitted from unique urchin-like binary hollow structure, complementing compositions, and favorable kinetics behaviors, FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy//PTCDA was expected to be promising in practical application. FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy was presodiated to approach the high initial Coulombic Efficiency (ICE) and raise the reversible capacity. PTCDA delivered a charge capacity ≈133 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>, while presodiated FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy demonstrated a charge capacity of ≈847 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> calculated according to anode mass (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0004">4a</a>), while FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy//PTCDA showed a charge capacity of 445 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a CE of 96.9% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0004">4b</a>). Reading from corresponding differential capacity versus voltage profiles (dQ dV<sup>−1</sup>) of FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy//PTCDA. An average operating voltage of ≈1.87&nbsp;V is achieved for the full cell (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0004">4c</a>). The full device showed highlighted rate performance with average charge capacities of ≈391.2, ≈362, ≈347.8, ≈311.9, ≈277.2, and ≈248.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0004">4d</a>), respectively, corresponding to a capacity degeneration of ≈36.5% with 40-fold increment of current density from 0.05 to 2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, benefiting from the enriched voids from flexible β-sheet Pcy and binary hollow structure, the excellent mechanical strength and ion conductivity as well as the favorable adjustable IHP configuration and the original Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics in liquid electrolyte, interfacial SEI and solid-state electrode. Except for the excellent rate performance, FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy//PTCDA also manifested exceptional cycling performance. Noticeably, after long durable 200 loops, a high charge capacity retention of 221.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> was achieved, corresponding to 71.4% to its pristine capacity (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403489-fig-0004">4e</a>) and showing a high CE of 99.1%. Based on the active material at 2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the energy density of the full device is computed to be ≈187.4&nbsp;Wh g<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 37.9&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>, even 66.3&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 3304.2&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>, which is commendable in comparing with previously reported work (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S38</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). implicating excellent Na<sup>+</sup> storage capability even at tough current rates. The homogenized Na<sup>+</sup> flux, the finely adjustable IHP distribution, the favorable urchin-hollow structure design with enriched free voices, and dynamic self-adaptive capacity to repair the structure deformation by virtue of the breaking and reconstruction of hydrogen bonds are charging. Thereby, these results unambiguously display the versatility of Pcy-modified FeS<sub>2</sub> complex in practical application in Na-based batteries and beyond.</p>

      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403489-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403489-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>The Pcy oligomers with a fine β-sheet configuration, high sodiophilicity sulfhydryl groups, carboxyls, aminoes, and modified binary hollow FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C structure (FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy) was delicately designed to achieve the high reversibility in SIBs for fast-charging and long durable sodium storage. Both experimental trials and theoretical simulation shows such FeS<sub>2</sub> complex displays the good structure integrity rapid Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics, excellent reactions, benefitting from the smart render of heterojunction, hollow matrix, and Pcy with elastic modulus via favorable α-helix to β-sheet conformation reconfiguration. The contracted vertical alignment of the zwitterionic Pcy molecular layer in the IHP is noticed, unlocking its protective role in directional inducer and excluding the free solvent molecules away from Na<sup>+</sup>, promoting the rapid Na<sup>+</sup> motion derived from it weakened Coulombic interaction with anions. Additionally, the self-adaptive capacity via the hydrogen breaking and reconstruction entrusts the superior electrochemical stability for FeS<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C@Pcy. Consequently, through the graft of Pcy, the ingenious reversibility, outstanding rate performance, and longevity in both half-cell and full cell has been approached. This work supplies new perspective into constructing the systematic protocol on the interaction of molecules and electrochemical species based on protein oligomers to entrust the anode material with highlighted reversibility and cycling performance even at a high rate.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
